<a id="t-8e11fbc221"></a>
## Thread: Searching Lists - was Soundex — 2 msgs

### Searching Lists - was Soundex

- **From:** James Gavan <jgavan@shaw.ca>
- **Date:** 2011-11-08T21:17:10-07:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<b9nuq.29601$0s1.9844@newsfe11.iad>`

```
This is in response to the information from Jerry and Pete provided on 
Soundex.

Firstly don't let us have a dissertation on the merits of C# rather than 
COBOL. This message is not promoting COBOL but showing a technique in 
the only language I have programmed in. And I think it is more effective 
than Soundex with only a 36% success rate. This is the first time I've 
looked at COBOL since December 2010 and will probably be the last.

INTRODUCTION :

Like the average user I have signed up occasionally in the past to 
access sites on the Web. Depending upon the site you can be presented 
with a Dropdown List of alphabetized country names. Although I'm near 
the top of the list it irritated me that I had to vertically scroll 
through some 20 - 30 countries before I got to 'Canada'. My observation 
was that I should be able to enter 'Can' which would take me straight to 
the element for 'Canada'. This is what this Keyboard Project is about.

Today I had to visit my family doctor, and very quickly he showed me how 
he can access patients Surnames and Firstname, obviously close to the 
technique I developed in 2003. Worth noting my doctor has some 22,000 
patients so volume doesn't appear to be a problem with his hardware 
configuration. (Obviously there's no way he probably sees half of the 
above on a regular basis. My own son is signed up with him and hasn't 
visited him yet !). If you want to see a parallel technique - take any 
application with an MS Help file format and follow the Help screen as 
you make different keystrokes.

Please note when referring to the mechanics I am using Micro Focus OO 
COBOL terminology. I have fine tuned the code written in 2003 to give 
what I describe below.

Basic System :

Unfortunately I can't show the screen dialog here because CLC wont 
accept attachments. So the screen looks as follows :-

--------------------------------------------------------------------------
(Dialog Title) :- EXAMPLE OF SEARCHING

  "Enter Cheese Name, one or several letters, Upper/Lowercase, and you 
can Insert or Backspace etc. When finished click on the Listbox Selection

{........entry field...........}

......................................................
		Listbox entries :

Ayshire			Scotland	000004
etc.......
Camembert		France
Gjetost			Norway		000009
Gorgonzola		Italy		000022
Gouda Aged		Holland		000034
Gouda Caraway		Holland		000035
Gouda Medium		Holland		000036
Gouda Young		Holland		000037
Gruyere			Switzerland	000100
Harvarti		Denmark		000202
Harvarti Caraway	Denmark		000203
etc........
Wensleydale		England		000095
..................................................

	<OK - Clear Selection>        <Exit>
-------------------------------------------------------
The system is a list (41 cheeses) of names hard coded into the Business 
Control program. 41 isn't many, but sufficient to test the methods.
In my example above, Wensleydale occupies the 41st Element.

the DB record :-

01 T2 redefines T1.
    05 T-record occurs MaxTable.
       10 ProductCode                  pic 9(06).
       10                              pic x.
       10 CheeseName                   pic x(20).
       10                              pic x.
       10 CheeseCountry                pic x(12).

The Collection procedure takes the above to put as elements into a 
Sorted Collection :-

01 ByName-record.
    05 CheeseName                pic x(20).
    05 Tab1                      pic x.
    05 CheeseCountry             pic x(12).
    05 Tab2                      pic x.
    05 ProductCode               pic 9(06).

b) The created collection, which is NOT edited, is passed to a Dialog 
for display in a Listbox with a vertical scroll bar.

c) Above the Listbox is an Entryfield to input descriptions you are 
searching on. The properties for the input entryfield you set up are :-

*>-----------------------------------------------------------
Method-id. "zCreateCheeseEntryfield".
*>-----------------------------------------------------------
Local-storage section.
78 p2ce-update                              value 64.
01 ls-event                                 pic x(4) comp-5.
01 ls-length                                pic x(4) comp-5.
Linkage section.
copy "dilogprm.new" replacing ==(tag)== by ==lnk==.

Procedure Division using lnk-Params.

  invoke self "getObjectFromId"
         using lnk-ID returning lnk-object

  invoke lnk-object "accessSystemEvents"

  if lnk-FontType <> zeroes
     invoke lnk-object "setfont" using os-Font(lnk-FontType)
  End-if

*> Dialog-ViewType

  move lnk-Length to ls-length

  if ls-length <> zeroes
     invoke lnk-object "setLength" using ls-length
  End-if

  initialize                ws-MethodRec
  move lnk-MethodName    to ws-MethodName
  move lnk-ClearType     to ws-ClearType
  move lnk-DisplayFormat to ws-DisplayFormat
  move lnk-ReturnType    to ws-ReturnType

  invoke os-Collection(1) "add" using lnk-object
  invoke os-Collection(2) "add" using ws-MethodRec

  move p2ce-Update to ls-event    ******************************
  set os-KeyboardObject to lnk-Object
  invoke lnk-object "setEventto" using
     ls-event, self, "returnKeyboardChars ",
          lnk-Field, ls-length

End Method "zCreateCheeseEntryfield".
*>-----------------------------------------------------------

***** Note the p2ce-update event above provided by Micro Focus - this is 
telling this object that the program wants all keystrokes made in the 
entryfield. The Entryfield accepts 1 - 20 into pic x(20), Upper/Lower 
case mixed. Apart from an initial start-up for Gained-Focus on the 
entryfield, neither Gained or Lost Focus events are used against the 
Entryfield or Listbox.

The event returned to the Control program from the Dialog object is :-

*>---------------------------------------------------------------
Method-id. "ReturnKeyboardChars".
*>---------------------------------------------------------------
Local-storage section.
01 ls-object                     object reference.
Linkage section.
01 lnk-Field                     pic x(4) comp-5.

Procedure Division using lnk-Field.

invoke os-Collection(2) "at"
        using lnk-Field returning ws-Methodrec
invoke os-Collection(1) "at"
        using Lnk-Field returning ls-object
invoke os-Caller ws-MethodName using ls-Object
*********
That last line above :-
os-Caller = SearchCheeses (the control program)
ws-Methodname :- EF-ENTRYFIELD
ls-Object = Object for the Entryfield
************************

Exit Method.
End Method "ReturnKeyboardChars".
*>---------------------------------------------------------------

CLASS - SearchCheeses
*>--------------------------------------------------------------
Method-id. "EF-ENTRYFIELD".
*>---------------------------------------------------------------
Local-storage section.
01 n                                pic x(4) comp-5.
01 ls-length                        pic x(4) comp-5.
01 ls-Text                          pic x(20).
01 ls-string                        object reference.
Linkage section.
01 lnk-Object                       object reference.

Procedure Division using lnk-Object.

initialize ls-text
move length of ls-Text to ls-length
invoke lnk-object "getText" returning ls-string
invoke ls-string "trimblanks" returning ls-string
invoke ls-string "getValueWithSize"
        using lnk-Length returning ls-text

*> Note : we are counting backwards for non-space characters.
*> Incrementing forwards using "Gouda Aged" would give a length
*> of 5 (Gouda) NOT 10 (Gouda Aged)


if     ls-text <> spaces
        move Function UPPER-CASE (ls-text) to ls-text
        compute ls-length = function length (ls-text)
        Perform varying n from ls-length by -1
                until ls-text(n:1) <> space
                OR  n = 1
        End-perform

        invoke os-CheeseDBI "matchRecords"
             using ls-text, n, returning ws-Index

        if   ws-Index <> zeroes
             initialize Dialog-Params
             set Field-LB-GenList to true
             move ws-Index to Dialog-Index
             set isSelected to true
             invoke os-Dialog "setSelectedUnselected"
                 using Dialog-Params
	**** Selected/Unselected highlights the element in the
		Listbox which matches current input key

        else invoke self "Message-Failure" using ls-Text
        End-if

End-if

Exit Method
End Method "EF-ENTRYFIELD".
*>---------------------------------------------------------------

CLASS - os-CheeseDBI - Cheese Database Interface

WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
*>-------------------------------------------------------------

01 ws-CollectionSize        pic x(4) comp-5.
01 ws-RecordLength          pic x(4) comp-5 value zeroes.
01 ByName-record.
    10 CheeseName            pic x(20).
    10 Tab1                  pic x.
    10 CheeseCountry         pic x(12).
    10 Tab2                  pic x.
    10 ProductCode           pic 9(06).

01 LastSearchKey.
    10 last-Index             pic x(4) comp-5 value 0.
    10 last-Name              pic x(20).

01 os-Collection            object reference value null.
*>-------------------------------------------------------------

*>-------------------------------------------------------------
Method-id. "matchRecords".  *> Method Revised Nov 2011
*>------------------------------------------------------------
Local-storage section.
01 n                            pic x(4) comp-5.
01 ls-Cheesename                pic x(20).
01 ls-string                    object reference.
01 P                            pic x(4) comp-5.
01 charx                        pic x.
Linkage section.
01 lnk-Text                     pic x(20).
01 lnk-Length                   pic x(4) comp-5.
01 lnk-index                    pic x(4) comp-5.

Procedure Division using lnk-Text, lnk-Length
                   returning lnk-Index.

*>-------------------------------------------------------------
*>  (Input) Lnk-Text   ------Search Table------------
*>                        Name     Index
*>
*>      C                 C          20
*>      CAM               CAM        56
*>      CA                CA         45
*>-------------------------------------------------------------

initialize lnk-Index
invoke os-Collection "size" returning ws-CollectionSize
move function UPPER-CASE (lnk-Text) to lnk-Text
*> The value of Last-Name is already stored as UPPERCASE

Evaluate true

     when        Last-Index = zeroes
                 move 1 to P

     when        lnk-Text > Last-Name
                 move Last-Index to P

     when other  move 1 to P

End-Evaluate


PERFORM varying n from P by 1 until n > ws-CollectionSize

    invoke os-Collection "at"
           using n returning ls-string
    invoke ls-string "getValuewithSize"
           using ws-RecordLength returning ByName-Record
    move CheeseName to ls-CheeseName
    move function UPPER-CASE (Cheesename) to ls-Cheesename

    Evaluate true

         *> First condition - you are searching on "G", and when
         *> you reach "H" in the sorted collection, no point in
         *> continuing

         when    ls-CheeseName(1:1) > lnk-Text(1:1)
                 EXIT METHOD

         when    lnk-Text(1:lnk-Length) =
                     ls-CheeseName(1:lnk-Length)
                 move n to Last-Index, lnk-Index
                 move lnk-Text(1:lnk-Length) to Last-Name
                 EXIT METHOD
    End-Evaluate

END-PERFORM

Exit Method.
End Method "matchRecords".
*>-------------------------------------------------------------

**** Some explanation of "MatchRecords" because this is where the search 
truly occurs. The following are only visually apparent when you use the 
M/F Animator to step through the code. Assume you were looking for 
"Cheddar" and you enter the three characters "che"; each 'current' 
string is sent individually to this method, that is :-

(1:1) = "c" - if the first record was 'Camembert' then its index
  	position is stored
(1:2) = "ch"
(1:3) = "che"

1:1 is going to find "c" and its index position is stored
1:2 uses the index position of 1:1 to start the second search
1:3 uses the index position of 1:2 to start the third search etc.....

Again not apparent visually, but each of the three 'keys' above 
highlights the appropriate entry in the List, but you only see the third 
or final highlight.

Of course if you have highlighted a record starting "che" then you are 
already close to 'Cheddar'. Without further entryfield input you can 
click on the appropriate cheese or use the vertical scroll bar. You can 
go backwards and forwards between entryfield input or scrolling when 
near the description you want.

Click a highlighted entry or an entry further down, not yet reached and 
you get a messagebox "You selected Product..... Name..... <PB-OK>".

If you key in characters which are not applicable, then you will get a 
failed message "Your key xxxxx not found <PB-OK>.

The above routine also tests for the last record. In my Collection the 
final index position is 41 = Wensleydale, so as a result of entering "w" 
it will highlight Wensleydale. You could add all characters for that 
name but it will still highlight Wensleydale. However if instead of 
entering "Wens" you enter "WenZ" - you will get a failed message.

That summarizes what the project is about.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------

COLLECTIONS :

Note that with Windows these can be created separately from CSC 
(collection support classes) or can be done within GUI Listbox Listview 
  or ComboBox Droplist controls themselves. I find this dual approach 
conflicting, and have restricted collection creation, changes, and 
searching to the CSC. The collection created by CSC, as amended, is 
passed to the Listbox giving a different object handle to the collection 
- but this is the same physical collection as the original - just two 
handles to the same object. Changes in one program that affect the 
Collection Object are also reflected in other programs using the same 
object.

Another reason for using only the CSC - collections can be useful 'in 
memory' tools, with automatic element increases as required. For 
example, Amazon etc. - select and put books into a shopping cart (an 
unordered collection) and subsequently turn the unordered collection 
into a sorted collection for GUI display/printing. Further sorted 
versions can be generated for warehouse picking lists, vehicle loads etc.

Background on the Micro Focus approach to Collections - and I am 
suggesting they may be paralleled in other OO languages.

- You create a Collection with or without a starting size. Where no size 
is indicated, M/F allocates a default size of 10 elements. Each time you 
want to add records, (exceeding current size), then M/F use a call to 
MALLOC to increase memory size for the collection. Keeping this topic 
brief, the final code at the end of this message is the source for 
TestSize.cbl.

VOLUMES.

I don't have a categoric answer to this one; it depends very much upon 
your hardware configuration and the requirements needed in your 
particular application.

The first thing to take into account is the size of your displayable 
element. My Byname record is minimal to be able to identify the entry = 
40 characters. So :-

# of Elements	Times	= Memory Requirement
---------------------------------------------
    500		40		 20,000
  1,000		,,		 40,000
  6,000		,,		 etc...
10,000		,,		 etc...
20,000		,,		800,000

What is an acceptable figure to you for memory usage ? Another factor is 
frequency of usage, infrequent, random or constantly being used by input 
clerks or professionals and their secretaries. Recall my family doctor 
has some 22,000 patients, searching on two fields Surname and First Name.

For performance if you have say, 2,000, 10,00 elements in the 
collection, and enter the name "Zebowski", you don't want the 
application to always start at the top "A" entry. If you look at the 
code for the method above "MatchRecords" you could adapt the entry for :-

01 LastSearchKey.
    10 last-Index             pic x(4) comp-5 value 0.
    10 last-Name              pic x(20).

to read :-

01 LastSearchKey occurs 26.
    10 last-Index             pic x(4) comp-5 value 0.
    10 last-Name              pic x(01).

and as a housekeeping routine read through the complete collection to 
get the first index position for the elements starting with "A", then 
"B" then etc. Store the result of this table into a reference file and 
access it to set up the table in "MatchRecords". Then if somebody wants 
to search on "Williamson" you access the first index for "W" in the 
revised table and start your search from the first element with "W". The 
possible permutations based on this idea are dependent upon how your 
Search is organized for your users.

You should remember that the example I've given above is NOT edited, so 
there is no re-positioning that occurs resulting from Adding or Deleting 
any records for a sorted collection. If your collection is created from 
a Database where Add/Changes/Deletions are occurring - then there is a 
problem - you will have to put on your thinking hat.

Another factor with a non-Edited collection is that you can use it in a 
multi-user mode. You can have a 'Master Program' which has the 
os-Master-Object created for the Collection. Then individual users 
access that one collection :-

invoke MasterProgram-Object "getCollectionID"  ( the os-Master-Object)
		returning os-Collection

The individual users then use their local version of the project but 
with their particular reference to os-Collection; different names, 
different object-references, but they are all accessing os-Master-Object.

As I wrote above, the Collection is NOT edited, so in theory at least, 
there should be no conflict between the routine for two different users 
queries. Again multi-user access will be affected by an Editable DB. You 
may have to introduce Lock-Mode procedures, just like you would for 
COBOL files.

Another approach would be to use a Treeview, replacing the LastSearchKey 
occurs 26. With a runthrough against the DB, keep a record of where each 
alphabetic letter starts. It should be written so that it is the user 
who determines groupings based on number of elements per group. The 
Treeview could then show something like the following :-

     <Root>
     :.........(Icon - Red Ball) [A - C]
     :
     ..........(Icon - Red Ball) [D - G]
     :
     ......... etc...

Based on volumes for the first or perhaps two characters, each element 
in the Treeview could hold the first index of the first/two characters. 
(Think in terms of MacDonald or McDonald if both forms are legitimate).
Calgary has, I think, the fifth largest Chinese community in N. America. 
We have six pages, four column per page for the Surname 'Lee' !!

Depending upon volumes, those groupings I show in the Treeview could be 
written to separate sub-Collections. Using icons - e.g.

	Red Ball 	- sub-Collection not yet created
	Green Ball 	- sub-Collection created

the groupings need only be created ONCE per day when they are first 
required. When created the Treeview shows a Green icon instead of a Red 
icon.

Let you mind jump around for further enhancements. Some will be 
blue-skying, others might be relevant and efficient.

Jimmy, Calgary AB

****************----------------------------------------**********

The code for Sizing collections follows :-

*>-------------------TestSize.cbl--------------------------------

class-control.
     TestSize                    is class "testsize"
     OrderedCollection           is class "ordrdcll"
     COBOLpicX                   is class "picx"
     .

working-storage section.

01 charx                    pic x.
01 n                        pic x(4) comp-5.
01 p                        PIC X(4) COMP-5.

01 ws-capacity              pic s9(9) comp-5.
01 ws-size                  pic s9(9) comp-5.
01 MyRecord.
    05 RecordName            pic x(20) value all "x".
    05 RecordIndex           pic zzzzz9.
01 ws-Length                pic x(4) comp-5.
01 NumberOfElements         pic x(4) comp-5.
01 NewValue                 pic x(4) comp-5 value 16000.
01 IndexValue               pic x(4) comp-5.

01 os-Collection-1          object reference.
01 os-Collection-2          object reference.
01 os-CurrentCollection     object reference.
01 os-Template              object reference.

Procedure Division.

move 17000 to NumberOfElements

move 1 to P
perform CREATE-COLLECTIONS
perform POPULATE
perform CHECK-SIZES-1

invoke os-CurrentCollection "deepFinalize"
             returning os-CurrentCollection

move 2 to P
perform CREATE-COLLECTIONS
perform POPULATE
perform CHECK-SIZES-2

invoke os-CurrentCollection "deepFinalize"
             returning os-CurrentCollection

STOP RUN.

CHECK-SIZES-1.

*> P(1)   Initial Size :     0   Size : 17000  Capacity : 20460

invoke  os-CurrentCollection "size"     returning ws-size
invoke  os-CurrentCollection "capacity" returning ws-Capacity

*> for P = 1 the following reduces the Capacity from
*> 20460 to 17000

*> You can "growTo" is a little misleading for a method
*> name because you can GrowUp or GrownDown depending upon
*> ws-Size. BUT, if your size was originally 5678 and you
*> enter a size of 5000, you will lose 678 elements - from the 
Collection, but it doesn't reflect in your database.

invoke  os-CurrentCollection "growTo"        *> NewValue = 16000
     using NewValue returning  os-CurrentCollection

invoke  os-CurrentCollection "size"     returning ws-size
invoke  os-CurrentCollection "capacity" returning ws-Capacity

*> P(1)   Initial Size :         Size : 17000  Capacity : 17000

*> If we now attempt to access elements : if IndexValue
*> = 14000 it will return that element showing the Index
*> number which I put in MyRecord. If however I move 16500
*> to IndexValue the following will abort :-

*>move 16500 to IndexValue
*>invoke  os-CurrentCollection "at"
*>          using IndexValue returning MyRecord
.

CHECK-SIZES-2.

*> P(2)   Initial Size : 17000   Size : 17000  Capacity : 17000

invoke  os-CurrentCollection "size"     returning ws-size
invoke  os-CurrentCollection "capacity" returning ws-Capacity
.

CREATE-COLLECTIONS.

*> SIZE     : Number of elements added to the collection
*> CAPACITY : Number of elements collection is capable of holding

move function length (MyRecord) to ws-length
invoke CobolPicx "newClass"
        using ws-Length returning os-template

Evaluate true

     when P = 1 move zeroes to ws-size
                invoke OrderedCollection "ofValues"
                 using os-template, ws-size
                       returning os-Collection-1
                 set os-CurrentCollection to os-Collection-1

     when P = 2 move 17000  to ws-size
                invoke OrderedCollection "ofValues"
                 using os-template, ws-size
                       returning os-Collection-2
                 set os-CurrentCollection to os-Collection-2
End-Evaluate.

POPULATE.

     perform varying n from 1 by 1 until n > NumberOfElements
         move n to RecordIndex
         invoke  os-CurrentCollection "add" using MyRecord
     end-perform

     invoke  os-CurrentCollection "size"     returning ws-size
     invoke  os-CurrentCollection "capacity" returning ws-Capacity
.

*> End Program.

*>----------------------------------------------------------------

	End of Message
```

#### ↳ Re: Searching Lists - was Soundex

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2011-11-10T15:46:55+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9i0s91F7h0U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<b9nuq.29601$0s1.9844@newsfe11.iad>`

```
James Gavan wrote:
> This is in response to the information from Jerry and Pete provided on
> Soundex.
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> is more effective than Soundex with only a 36% success rate.

I haven't tried the code, but I did look through it and it seems to me that 
it doesn't DO what Soundex does.

It's like comparing apples and bananas; both useful but you wouldn't make an 
apple pie with bananas...

Using a progressive keystroke search is NOT the same as searching for things 
based on what they SOUND like.

For example, it won't pick up Caerphilly if the user enters it as 
"Karefilly".  Soundex (modified as HeyBub suggested) will.

(If I missed something here and it actually will pick this up, please accept 
my apologies and point out where it does it.)

The code posted is interesting but these days the controls themselves have 
progressive keystroke search capability and there's really no need to spell 
it all out.

For myself, if I wanted to do this manually (and I can't imagine why I 
would) and I HAD to do it in COBOL (and I can't imagine why I would) :-),
I'd use a bound list. Then just changing the resultset is automatically 
reflected on the screen.

If you bind your drop down control to an ADO resultset and pass your entry 
field to a stored procedure as a LIKE parameter you can do the whole lot (in 
COBOL) and watch the drop down list change instantly as you type (showing 
only the entries which qualify against what you typed - the list should get 
shorter as you type more characters...), without any further effort on your 
part...

But it STILL won't do what Soundex does...:-)

I get the feeling this was more about using collections than actually 
finding homonyms. The idea of going through a collection to find the start 
of each letter in the alphabet then write that to a file, is repugnant to 
me. Why not use a node collection and load the 26 nodes directly to a 
treeview?

I guess there are many ways to skin a cat and most of us will have our own 
preferences.

Pete.

<snipped extensive interesting code>
```

#### ↳ Re: How do I get a posting removed?

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2011-11-11T14:09:21+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9i3au3F1o9U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<502fa981-fcf1-43b9-804f-9e032d8ccabe@u28g2000yqb.googlegroups.com>`

```
wjl_xyz wrote:
> How do I get a posting removed?

As Allodoxaphobia astutely pointed out, once your post has been propagated 
by the news server, you have very little chance of removing it from the 
cyber space. Even if you get it off the Google server, it will still remain 
on hundreds, possibly thousands, of other servers...

Theoretically it would be possible to trace the server logs and remove 
something from everywhere it was posted but I know of no software that does 
that (probably in the CIA domain :-)), and I'm almost certain that Google 
would accept no responsibility for servers other than their own. (Why should 
they? It was YOU who posted...:-))

The feature of message propagation is what makes these forums so useful.

Efforts have been directed over years to getting messages propagated, not to 
recalling them.

Sometimes it is spooky... I have found things I posted in all innocence 
years ago, popping up on web sites I never heard of and certainly never 
posted to. Investigation showed they had picked up stuff I wrote from a 
Usenet feed (once its on Usenet it is, in reality, in the Public Domain, and 
it's no good bleating about your intellectual property and the fact that 
what you said was not intended for circulation...)

BOTTOM LINE:

If you post to Usenet, whatever you post will be propagated into cyberspace 
within a few hours. Your only chance is to remove it IMMEDIATELY  before it 
has a chance to propagate, and, of course, you can only do that if the 
server permits it (as Google apparently does...)

Given that what you say is out there for ever, it is probably wise to think 
BEFORE posting :-)

I can't say I have always followed this rule because sometimes emotion can 
get the better of you, but nowadays I try to postpone clicking SEND if I 
know I am upset. Sleep on it... THEN send it :-)

Pete.
```

## Thread: conversion from Microfocus NetExpress COBOL to Fujitsu netCOBOL.net — 50 this month / 90 total

```
Am 13.11.2011 17:59, schrieb SkippyPB:
> There remains a large number of schools that teach Cobol.  There has
> been a resurgance in Cobl classes at the University and Trade school
> level.  For a list of some, see
> http://www.mainframes.com/schools.htm

   These are 37 institutions, if I counted right, for a country (USA) 
with about 300 million inhabitants, and some of the institutions 
supposedly teaching COBOL are outside of that country.

   I was, of course, especially interested by the entries of 
institutions in Germany. The link given for the Leipzig university leads 
to an information block about their IMB z9 mainframe, which is called 
"jedi", and one does actually find in one page that there is a COBOL 
compiler installed. But when one tries to find COBOL courses from the 
main page of the informatics institute which operates that mainframe, 
the search result is NIL. Try yourself (in English) at
<http://www.informatik.uni-leipzig.de/ifi/en/search.html>

   The same applies to the Fachhochschule Erlangen (University of 
applied sciences, they call themselves in English). Here is the plan for 
the study of "Wirtschaftsinformatik" (commercial informatics), which is 
the most susceptible to relate to COBOL:
 > 
<http://www.hs-esslingen.de/en/the-university/faculties/engineering-management/study-programmes/management-and-information-systems/overview-of-bachelors-degree-program.html>

  The courses in software development point to a book on Java, but do 
not mention COBOL. You can also use the seach facility at the upper 
right corner of that page.

   The domain of the third institution in Europe (and German speaking), 
a "Hï¿½here Technische Lehranstalt" in Vienna, "http://www.htl-tex.ac.at/" 
is not found by the DNS. Maybe it does not exist, or under another name. 
There are lots of "Hï¿½here Technische Lehranstalt" in Austria...

   I guess the reality of COBOL teaching in the other 35 or so 
institutions listed on that webpage will evaporate as quickly as the 
ones which I searched.

   I do not want to drive you into a depression -- I learned COBOL long 
time ago, and liked to work in it -- but we have to face the reality, 
which is that COBOL is a language of the past, a dinosaur.


Cheers,
L.W.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: conversion from Microfocus NetExpress COBOL to Fujitsu netCOBOL.net

_(thread depth: 11)_

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2011-11-16T00:54:57+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9if28kFaobU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<1826132.525.1318451603192.JavaMail.geo-discussion-forums@vbau1> <7411645a-c787-437b-8840-3b3b65209774@ff5g2000vbb.googlegroups.com> <kS5pq.2$zC6.0@en-nntp-15.dc1.easynews.com> <9gkd1tFudeU1@mid.individual.net> <b7e85c5e-dc23-42bb-9a0f-90a48758b951@gy7g2000vbb.googlegroups.com> <9gmcg1Fc37U1@mid.individual.net> <89ba98ef-bd73-4f4b-834e-20911e4ef4cb@u37g2000prh.googlegroups.com> <4ebf928b$0$4150$6e1ede2f@read.cnntp.org> <9i9sq0FfgbU1@mid.individual.net> <cotvb71tqrhj4btpkhpl4rdct9i27bn80n@4ax.com> <4ec193d8$0$4150$6e1ede2f@read.cnntp.org>`

```
L�ko Willms wrote:
> Am 13.11.2011 17:59, schrieb SkippyPB:
>> There remains a large number of schools that teach Cobol.  There has
…[40 more quoted lines elided]…
>
I don't think anyone HAS to face that reality, Lueko.

And there are people here who simply won't. :-)

That's OK

In time, the reality becomes apparent and it doesn't really matter whether 
that is today, tomorrow or next year.

Bill G. will try and get and get it taught one more time,  and cannot 
understand why no-one is listening.

Old-time IBM mainframers who have no use or understanding for objects and 
layers will refuse to let it go until, eventually, they are all gone and 
their platforms are supplanted  by, or subsumed into,  the ever increasing 
network.

People who make a living selling COBOL compilers will continue talking it up 
as if it was still relevant. (While they are looking for ways to diversify 
out of it...)

None of it really matters. I predicted it would be gone as a viable 
commercial development language by 2015.

I was wrong.

It has already happened.

After being in the top 3 for many years, COBOL is not even in the top 20 
development languages.

http://www.tiobe.com/index.php/content/paperinfo/tpci/index.html

Although it has picked up a few places since last year it is ironic to note 
that Assembly Language is more popular (just...) than COBOL, which 
supplanted it for general use around 50 years ago. I guess what goes around 
comes around... :-)

Another site that may be of interest (and is relevant to COBOL) :

http://www.rackspace.com/cloud/blog/2011/05/17/infographic-evolution-of-computer-languages/

But none of it is REALLY important.

(It is fair to ask whether program language popularity matters anyhow...I 
guess if the skill you have is in great demand you have more chance of 
staying employed, but, on the other hand, if the skill you have is not in 
great demand then you can charge more for it when it IS needed :-))

If you work on a site that uses COBOL, then COBOL is important to you. If 
your career is drawing to a close, then the future of that site, and whether 
they stay with COBOL or move off it, is not of any significance to you.

If you are a young person looking for a career in programming then you won't 
need Lueko or me to tell you that COBOL will be a pointless waste of time. 
If you apply yourself instead to other more relevant languages and 
techniques, it is pretty easy to pick up a simple procedural paradigm like 
COBOL if/when the need arises. (Unfortunately, the converse is not true and 
history has shown that people immersed in COBOL, generally are not capable 
of moving easily to an object based paradigm. They tend to invent reasons 
not to and support each other in their general denigration of Object 
Oriented Programming as being unnecessary (tell that to the 90% of the World 
that runs on it...) and just a re-invention of "modular programming", which 
it isn't...)

Although my company started out insisting people move off COBOL, we have 
modified that position and today we don't really care whether our clients 
opt to stay with COBOL or move to something else, AS LONG as they are using 
Objects and Layers in the .Net environment. The "layers" part means a three 
tier solution, with separation between the Presentation Layer (User 
Interface), the Business Logic, and the Data Access Layer.

Our Tools currently generate the Data Access Layer automatically at the same 
time as they generate the new Relational Database from the existing COBOL 
indexed file base. We are currently looking at getting the Presentation 
Layer also separated and generated automatically.

My interest in this has been stimulated with the technical previews for 
Windows 8. The new Metro interface is entirely XAML based and if people have 
separation between their Business Logic and their Presentation Layer it is 
not too hard to generate a XAML equivalent of their exisiting screens. 
(Metro is a touch based, cross platform interface. It supports mouse and 
keyboard but touch is primary. Metro runs on ANY windows platform; desktop, 
web, tablet, mobile phone, without any coding changes being required. Expect 
to hear more about it, and XAML, in the next few years.)

Although I would not recommend anyone stay with COBOL long term, mostly 
people find out for themselves when they get the maintenance bill for their 
expensive COBOL compiler and then realise they could do the same job with a 
better free tool from Microsoft.

 We offer an option to people who are prepared to "bite the bullet" and move 
off COBOL during or shortly after Conversion/Migration. There is then no 
need to buy a .Net COBOL compiler, but we really don't care if they don't 
take that option. It is about having a choice.

As far as the popularity of programming languages goes, don't be surprised 
to see JavaScript trending upwards over the next few years. The combination 
of HTML5/CSS and JavaScript as being "quick build" XAML generators is being 
touted currently by Microsoft for developing Win 8 applications.

In the Microsoft world, the distinction between desktop applications and web 
based ones started blurring with products like Silverlight and WPF (both of 
which generate XAML and both of which can be built for the web or the desk). 
Now it looks as if  these products will become merged under the HTML5 
banner. (Silverlight has already been discontinued at the same time as Adobe 
discontinued Flash, its main competitor.)

(Note that if you already develop for the Web using ASP.NET and server side 
"code behinds" in C# (as I do... the COBOL21 and PRIMA sites are developed 
in this way), or  C++, or VB.Net, these will still work in HTML5, but now 
you can bring the same "code behind" approach to the desktop and other 
surfaces. Because it is objects that are actually wired up, the programming 
language is unimportant. It is all about layers and objects...The JavaScript 
can be run as normal client side script served up on the page, or it can be 
used for "code behind" and run on the server.)

It will be interesting to see what the winner of the Language Wars will be, 
although, as I tried to outline above, it no longer matters once you are 
using objects.

It won't be COBOL.

Pete.
```

The following is a combined response to both Fritz and Lueko.

There are some things anyone reading this should bear in mind:

1. Arguing whether COBOL is still viable is completely pointless. It is for 
some people; it isn't for others. And some of us are now in positions where 
we really don't care what language is used to build objects.

2. I use Microsoft tools every day and I develop for people who use 
MicroSoft operating systems on their computers. I am not employed by MS, I 
have no particular allegiance to them, but I do appreciate that they have 
made my job easier. In my dealings with them I have found them to be 
responsive, helpful, and knowledgeable. I cannot say the same about some 
other computer companies I have dealt with. YMMV.

Now read on... :-)

L�ko Willms wrote:
> Am 15.11.2011 19:12, schrieb Fritz Wuehler:
>
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
> companies doing it.

You can put your head as deeply into the sand as you wish, but the FACT is 
that an increasing number of Companies are moving away from COBOL. That 
includes mainframe sites.

>
>> You'll have to get rid of
>> FORTRAN, PL/I and assembler until the mainframe goes Java.

And you don't think that's going to happen? :-) Look around... I haven't 
seen any commercial sites running Fortran since around 1968 and I know 
personally of three IBM Mainframe sites  (all in the UK) that moved off PL/1 
years ago.


>
>   Especially speaking of IBM mainframes ... as far as I can see, IBM
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
>> Not everywhere, people are still hiring.

Tell Bill.

And I don't really see any need to defend my statement. When something goes 
form being in the top 3 to being 25th, it is reasonable to say it is not 
viable. Eeven if it is not quite extinct (and it is not 2015 yet...) there 
are many (around 24 to be exact) development languages which people think 
are better.

>
>   I know. Companies do not lightly give up all the investment in
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> retire to profit from their old age pensions.

I agree. But what actually happens is that they then review the whole cost 
of maintaining COBOL into the future and the bean counters tell them to bin 
it. As long as nothing rocks the boat, things will tick over fine; as soon 
as someone retires or they can't get a replacement the whole issue is 
brought into sharper focus.
>
>> Yawn...really now Pete. That list is for people who think a PC is a
>> computer. They don't have any idea that companies have things like
>> mainframes, minis and servers.

That is a little bit arrogant, Fritz.  There are some very capable people 
who really DO understand IT, working in places where they don't run 
mainframes. (I have worked with some of them and learned much...)
>
>   What is today a "mini"?
>
>   Does Data General still exist? Wang? Nixdorf?

Good questions, Lueko.
>
>>>>  Although I would not recommend anyone stay with COBOL long term,
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> to do is sell, sell, sell...

I don't think that is fair. It is a different Company than it was 10 years 
ago. You could argue that three of their major development tools would be an 
IDE, a COMPILER, and a RDBMS. Many companies in the business of IT Tools see 
these as bread and butter. (And charge like wounded bulls for them...)

Microsoft have several IDE type tools (Visual Studio, Expression Blend, and 
some specialist IDEs for other areas), at least three major compilers (C#, 
VB.Net, C++), and two RDBMS (one lightweight (Access) and one industrial 
strength (SQL Server)), and ALL of them are available free, although some 
will require a fee after 60 days. The three most important ones for me are 
Visual Studio, C#, and SQL Server. ALL of these are unreservedly FREE in the 
Express Editions. And, contrary to what you might think, the Express 
Editions are more than adequate for most development needs. The latest R2 of 
SQL Server 2008 is a completely free download and use. All they ask is that 
you register it. There is no cost to do so and they never hassle you. There 
are NO runtime fees or fees of any other kind; it is a FREE product. So is 
Visual Studio Express and so is C#. The only reason you might require a paid 
license would be if you need a high performance multi-server industrial 
repository with all the infrastructure that goes with that. Most people 
don't and if they did they would probably go to Azure and run in the Cloud.

As for "sell, sell, sell", do you know of any company that doesn't do that? 
Sales are a necessary part of staying in business.:-)

I can only speak from my own actual experience. Currently I'm at school 
learning new stuff that I will need to facilitate movement to Win 8. (mainly 
XAML and background concepts on User Interfaces, Graphic Design, User 
Experience, and such. I hope to produce better web sites and application 
interfaces by the time I am finished.)  For "extra credit" (you need to 
acquire evaluation credit to progress through the course as succeeding 
levels are only available when you pass the lower levels... it is kind of 
fun really. I flunked a unit this morning and was so annoyed I immediately 
re-did it and passed :-))  you can do a few units on Windows Phone so I'll 
probably do that too. The lessons are excellent, I'm enjoying the learning 
experience and becoming aware of stuff I had no idea existed. The videos I 
am doing are free from Microsoft as part of their Toolbox program. At no 
point has anyone started banging the drum for Microsoft and at no point have 
I felt compelled to purchase anything.

Having said that, it is on the cards that I'll purchase Expression Blend but 
no one is pressing me to and it is absolutely worth the money. Best tool I 
have ever seen for what it does.

>
>> That doesn't make any sense. Microsoft is not the only company and
>> Windows on Intel is not the only platform in the world.

Sure, to save me having to put disclaimers on future posts can you take it 
as read that I am developing for the Microsoft environment, specifically 
.Net and Windows 8? I have a passing interest in other platforms but it is 
only passing.

Does my statement make sense now? :-)

(Note that I don't require you to make the same statement regarding your 
employment on IBM mainframes; I can deduce it from your post and am not 
offended by it.)

>
>   Sure, it is threatened by iOS and Android operating systems.
>
You have no idea how ludicrous that statement is. Android may not even be 
legal :-)

There is no threat to Microsoft interests from either of these quarters. 
They will probably never gain the share of the mobile device market that 
Apple and Google are getting but it doesn't matter. They are producing 
something that will run across ALL platforms without code changes. People 
who like what they have at work will possibly want it on their phone. People 
who have a phone will definitely want the same kind of interfaces on what 
they have at work. Buying Microsoft will guarantee that, buying other brands 
may not. The Metro interface will decide the fate of the company. If it 
fails then Microsoft will be in serious trouble. But what I've seen so far 
does not look to me like a failed product. When I get a few minutes I'll 
post a demo of what I'm talking about.

In five years time, see if you still think they are "threatened" by Android 
and iOS. That is a user perception. It isn't shared by anyone I know at MS.


>> But if you use that "better
>> free tool" from Microsoft you're stuck on Windows on Intel. I'd
>> rather be stuck on the mainframe.

We are all happy to be "stuck" on whatever we are comfortable with. I liked 
your statement, it was fair and honest and it made me smile :-)

Pete

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: conversion from Microfocus NetExpress COBOL to Fujitsu netCOBOL.net

_(thread depth: 17)_

- **From:** Lüko Willms <lueko.willms@domain.invalid>
- **Date:** 2011-11-17T11:19:24+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4ec4dfad$0$4151$6e1ede2f@read.cnntp.org>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<3fc2a950487d411bb46e8e26ef74078c@msgid.frell.theremailer.net>`
- **References:** `<4ec3897f$0$4150$6e1ede2f@read.cnntp.org> <3fc2a950487d411bb46e8e26ef74078c@msgid.frell.theremailer.net>`

```
Am 17.11.2011 06:14, schrieb Fritz Wuehler:
>>>>     The mainframes you are thinking of -- are they very different from a
>>>>> >  >>  >    multi-CPU machine running microcode on standard Intel or AMD CPUs?
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
> have some purpose for asking it?

   The purpose was clearly visible: to give a hint on the changes in 
computing over the past decades, the creeping demise of COBOL being one 
of its aspects.

   As far as I can see, there are three mainframe manufacturers left 
over from "IBM and the Seven Dwarfs": Unisys, Fujitsu (carrying on the 
former Siemens BS2000 line, i.e. RCA's TSOS), and of course IBM.

   In my view, only IBM would be able to build bespoke CPUs for their 
zOS machines, but their byte architecture would fit perfectly in the 
byte architecture of Intel/AMD CPUs, so it would be easy for IBM to use 
such CPUs, and much more economically than building bespoke chips. 
Unisys with their 36 bit and 48 bit mainframe architectures have much 
more problems with that.


Cheers,
L.W.

L�ko Willms <lueko.willms@domain.invalid> wrote:

>    As far as I can see, there are three mainframe manufacturers left 
> over from "IBM and the Seven Dwarfs": Unisys, Fujitsu (carrying on the 
> former Siemens BS2000 line, i.e. RCA's TSOS), and of course IBM.

All you need is IBM. In almost 40 years in the business I haven't ever
worked on anything else and I have never been in a shop that didn't have an
IBM machine. I have seen plenty of brand X disks and tapes, but never an
Amdahl or Unisys or Fujitsu box. 

>    In my view, only IBM would be able to build bespoke CPUs for their 
> zOS machines, but their byte architecture would fit perfectly in the 
> byte architecture of Intel/AMD CPUs,

This statement is so totally wrong I don't know where to begin.

IBM ISA is nothing like Intel/AMD, nothing like POWER or any RISC ISA on the
market, and nothing like any other common microprocessor ISA.

IBM *already* builds CPUs for z/OS and z/OS will *only* run on those CPUs
and could *never* be ported to any other ISA. Get the Principles of
Operations Manual for z/OS and the ISA handbook for POWER and the Intel
or AMD processor manuals, open them up side by side, and stop taking
drugs. Your comment is totally out of line with reality.

> so it would be easy for IBM to use such CPUs, and much more economically
> than building bespoke chips.  Unisys with their 36 bit and 48 bit
> mainframe architectures have much more problems with that.

Word size is the least of the problems. You do realize the whole OS, the
assembler, and all the compilers are based on a specific ISA and to get
all that to work with any other ISA, even if there was anything similar in the
world, which there is not, would require a total rewrite? 

You do realize IBM's ISA is big-endian, and Intel/AMD are little-endian? You
do realize all of the disk and tape files and data base contents would be
instantly worthless since IBM's native data types other than integer aren't
available on any other ISA? Intel/AMD can't operate on IBM packed decimal or
floating point data even if they could fix the endianness problem which
itself is far from trivial. Right now you can still read data from files
created in 1964. Under your ingenius plan 50 years of data is instantly
worthless.

Oh, you thought z/OS was a toy like UNIX? No, it isn't. It's a real OS,
optimised to a specific ISA and specific hardware and can't be ported
without a total rewrite of the OS, compilers, assembler, and all the vendor
products ever written. That's a few trillion dollars of R&D and you think
they can do that all over again in a week and use chips from toy computers?
Think again.

Like I said, your question shows you have no idea at all what you're talking
about.

```
On Nov 18, 5:09 am, Lüko Willms <lueko.wil...@domain.invalid> wrote:
> Am 17.11.2011 16:44, schrieb Nomen Nescio:
>
…[34 more quoted lines elided]…
> is the usual weighing of processing speed vs. development cost.

There have been some CPUs which could be microcoded to emulate other
CPUs. These were designed from the ground up to do so. Generally they
turned out to be much slower than the ones they were emulating.
Current Intel CPUs cannot be microcoded in this way, it won't change
the instruct set or byte order.

IBM mainframes have been emulated in software, for example the IBM XT/
370 which used a couple of addin boards with a couple of 68000
processors plus some specialised memory accessing hardware for virtual
memory. The 68000s ran emulation software that could in turn run 370
software - very slowly compared to a real machine.

Hercules did write an emulator using top-end Intel based systems. It
seems that it can get to the performance of an entry level zSeries,
but like you can't get 9 women to have a baby in a month, a rack full
of Intel CPUs isn't necessarily a replacement for a mainframe.


> > Oh, you thought z/OS was a toy like UNIX?
>
>    You know that you can run UNIX (or is it Linux?) on a IBM z machine?
>
>    Your dismissal of Unix is quite telling.

Z series can run dozens of Linux instances alongside other workload.
These are versions compiled for the machine.

You can run MS-DOS on a Linux machine using DOSBOX, but that does not
make MS-DOS an equivalent to Unix/Linux.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: conversion from Microfocus NetExpress COBOL to Fujitsu netCOBOL.net

_(thread depth: 20)_

- **From:** Fritz Wuehler <fritz@spamexpire-201111.rodent.frell.theremailer.net>
- **Date:** 2011-11-26T23:15:06+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<01ae72a3eec2afc59f22839a9b205a1a@msgid.frell.theremailer.net>`
- **References:** `<4ec63b3a$0$286$14726298@news.sunsite.dk>`

```
Fred Mobach <fred@mobach.nl> wrote:

> I have seen a number of Siemens mainframes running OS'en like TSOS,
> BS1000 and BS2000. Not their BS3000 IBM-compatible OS from Siemens AG
> (historical), which was removed after IBM started a trial on that. But
> on some of those systems IBM's OS'es could run (because the Assembler
> instructions were equal ?).

I realize other companies make IBM clones, some of my coworkers are ex
hardware guys from Amdahl and Unisys. My point to the idiot Juko is those
clones have no market share. I've been in hundreds of installations and
never seen one and AFAIK none of the customers for any of the companies
I've worked for had one either. Juko's talent for misquoting has messed up
the thread. Your question at the end is based on his misquoting and from not
reading what I wrote but rather what he claimed I wrote.

> While not comparable on speed Hercules seems to do well in their job of
> emulation (see www.hercules-390.org).

Speed is an issue for big shops that process millions of transactions an
hour. Hercules is excellent for development and testing but it cannot
support mainframe workloads on available Intel boxes, they can't support the
I/O or terminal networks or coupling facilities, etc. etc. etc.

Another issue is it is not IBM hardware and it's not 100% compatible and IBM
doesn't license anything to run on it. If you read the Hercules mailing list
you will see many errors reported, some are not really errors but some
are. None of that happens on real hardware. And nobody is running production
on Hercules because it's against IBM's license terms. I would not trust my
production on it. It's fine for development on older (out of production
versions) of MVS. People have problems with newer z/VM and the software
development of Hercules will not be able to keep up with System Z.

Hercules runs on cheap hardware that doesn't have the RAS features of IBM's
machines that stay up for years and can hot swap boards and other
hardware. IBM mainframe DASD is far better than the best SAS drives you can
get with a SAN from Oracle. There are other issues besides emulation itself.

If IBM would license their OS to run on Hercules I could see some
non-critical work being run on Intel or SPARC boxes but there are many other
issues such as how to connect DASD, ESCON, etc. and other issues we don't
even know about yet.

There were other solutions like the P/390 and Flex/ES but they were taken
off the market by IBM because it was possible to run small workloads on them
and possibly threaten their hardware sales although performance and
reliability issues were present on those devices as well. The P/390 had a
real 390 processor on board. Flex/ES was an emulator.

Juko's claim was about hardware CPU emulation and I refuted that. In fact
there have been many instances of chipmakers using hardware emulation to
support prior versions of code, architecture etc. and very few of them were
acceptable, even when you're talking about chips from the same manufacturer.
So far not many companies are willing to do the R&D or corp espionage
involved in cloning mainframe CPUs, it's a few billion USD in R&D to get to
the point they are at now. The P/390 wasn't emulation, it was a real 390
architecture chip running on a PC chassis. It had some of the same issues as
other solutions like not being able to connect to a CF and had no ESCON
etc. The Flex/ES box had the same issues as Hercules but had no community
support. Neither is available now.

You are talking about software emulation, which is far far cheaper and
simpler, but has performance, RAS, and compatibility problems. A bigger
issue is neither software nor hardware emulation is going to keep pace with
System Z at the present rate of development, realizing this kind of hardware
development pace is much greater than historically for the architecture. If
you spent money cloning a 370 or a 390 you had many years of product
life. If you try that with z/OS you'll find the expense much to great. IBM
is making sure the OS that runs on your box today will not run on that box 3
years from now. Only manufacturing giants can afford the R&D and
manufacturing to support that. Intel and AMD might be able to, and they
might not. Their business model is totally different, they sell many cheap
things rather than few expensive things. They haven't ever shown the
interest nor the ability to enter the IBM clone market.
```

You have now! Glad I wasn't imagining things. Looks like UNIVAC bought out

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: conversion from Microfocus NetExpress COBOL to Fujitsu netCOBOL.net

_(thread depth: 27)_

- **From:** Lüko Willms <lueko.willms@domain.invalid>
- **Date:** 2011-11-30T08:57:18+01:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4ed5e1d3$0$4150$6e1ede2f@read.cnntp.org>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<9932d0946207982b780a03961012dd4c@msgid.frell.theremailer.net>`
- **References:** `<9jk8hdFrckU3@mid.individual.net> <9932d0946207982b780a03961012dd4c@msgid.frell.theremailer.net>`

```
Am 29.11.2011 22:01, schrieb Fritz Wuehler:
>> I did IBM up thru the 4300 series and Univac from the 1100 and I never saw
>> >  anything compatable between them.  I have never seen a Univac mainframe
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> the RCA Spectra line in 1971.

   Exactly. Siemens also continued that line with their BS2000 systems.

 > The UNIVAC I used was in late 1970 early 1980 timeframe.
 > I didn't do any system programming so I don't know what OS
> it used.

   That could be this RCA inheritance, or the 90/30, 9400, 9700, or 
whatever. The larger systems ran the Univac version of TSOS, which was 
called VS/9, the smaller systems had their own operating systems, e.g. 
OS/3.

 > I wrote application code and I know it used the 360 or 370
> instruction set.

   That's what I explained in an earlier contribution to this thread: 
CPU-Assembler compatible but not OS compatible. Only the latter would 
qualify as an IBM clone, destined and able to run IBM's operating 
systems. Neither Sperry Univac nor Borroughs ever tried to enter that 
market.


Cheers,
L.W.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: conversion from Microfocus NetExpress COBOL to Fujitsu netCOBOL.net

_(thread depth: 27)_

- **From:** HansJ <hans.igel@googlemail.com>
- **Date:** 2011-11-30T03:25:52-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<a425b3eb-f0cd-4e27-bfad-4ef95fa089e8@20g2000yqa.googlegroups.com>`
- **References:** `<9jk8hdFrckU3@mid.individual.net> <9932d0946207982b780a03961012dd4c@msgid.frell.theremailer.net>`

```
On 29 Nov., 22:01, Fritz Wuehler
<fr...@spamexpire-201111.rodent.frell.theremailer.net> wrote:
> > I did IBM up thru the 4300 series and Univac from the 1100 and I never saw
> > anything compatable between them.  I have never seen a Univac mainframe
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
> instruction set.

Fritz,

the 90/60, 90/70 and 90/80 where running VS/9 and are - as you said -
originating from RCA. The "IBM assembler" was basically supported, so
IBM assembler code was easily portable. The 90/30 running OS/3 was
supporting the IBM assembler (a few differences) as well, but the OS
was completely different.

If I recall it correctly, also the 9400 had a very similar assembler
instruction set as IBM.

Regards Hans
```

```
On 28 Nov., 16:25, billg...@cs.uofs.edu (Bill Gunshannon) wrote:

Bill,

you are missing quite a few systems, the 9400 series running OS/4, the
90/60, 90/70, 90/80 series running VS/9 (as Lueko mentioned), the
90/30, 90/40 and the system 80 series with a number of different
system running OS/3.

Not to mention the systems that have been available before the low end
9200 and 9300 was introduced. The 9200 and 9300 used to run a TOS
(Tape Operating System - if I recall it correct).

To get back to the COBOL part, VS/9 and OS/3 definitely had a COBOL
compiler from the beginning, I'm not sure about OS/4, at least I did
only write in assembler on that platform.

Regards Hans

Howard,

you are mixing up the 90/30 and the 90/60 (etc.). The 90/30 was a pure

that was a failure.

<a id="t-59611ff569"></a>
## Thread: [OT] Whatever Happened To... ? — 12 this month / 14 total

### [OT] Whatever Happened To... ?

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2011-11-14T17:58:05+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<j9rkrd$86d$1@reader1.panix.com>`

```

My memory is, admittedly, porous... but the other day I was reminded of 
something that someone posted here and was wondering about how things 
went.

The 'something' was the moving of the organisation to what today's 
youngsters called a 'projectised' environment, the result of which would 
be that the programmers would all be assigned to a pool and allocated to 
various managers for the completion of projects.

The 'someone' I don't recall... but I do seem to remember that nobody, 
myself included, had much positive to say about such a scheme.

Anyone know how things developed?

Thanks much.

DD
```

verifiability, that you have heard (flip the coin) nothing good about the 
results...

... and/or you've heard no bad results of the reorganisation, as well.

DD
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Whatever Happened To... ?

- **From:** docdwarf@panix.com ()
- **Date:** 2011-11-15T12:29:51+00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<j9tlvv$i2q$1@reader1.panix.com>`
- **References:** `<j9rkrd$86d$1@reader1.panix.com> <1ea3b9fe-656b-43eb-8ae7-6a02a8d02094@q16g2000yqn.googlegroups.com>`

```
In article <1ea3b9fe-656b-43eb-8ae7-6a02a8d02094@q16g2000yqn.googlegroups.com>,
Alistair Maclean  <alistair.j.l.maclean@gmail.com> wrote:
>On Nov 14, 5:58?pm, docdw...@panix.com () wrote:
>>
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
>Isn't that Matrix Management?

I'm not quite sure, Mr Maclean.  As I understand it (from all the Latest 
Literature with which I am familiar) a company is, typically, confronted 
with two opposing business needs: the need to Just Do Stuff and the need 
to complete projects.  A project, by definition, is a temporary and 
limited series of activities which produce an unique product or service 
while Just Doing Stuff is how the company actually fulfills its raison 
d'etre, ie, Make Money.

Take as an example a delivery company.  The functional aspect of the 
organisation is fairly straightforward: stuff comes in the door, gets 
loaded onto trucks, goes out the door and delivered.  A vital function in 
delivery is routing, the determining of the most efficient/least expensive 
path to track for a particular load of goods.

Routing used to be done by folks with lists and maps and cups of coffee 
and endless streams of cigarettes.  Computers have replaced a lot of that.

So... when the project arises to switch over routing methodologies from 
the 'Louie with a cup of mud and a Lucky Strike' to 'Pat at a keyboard' 
two things need to be done simultaneously: the company has to keep moving 
goods (retaining its functionality) and the company has to allocate 
personnel and resources towards the completion of the project of 
computerisation.

Just about all companies have a balance between these two 
resource-competing needs, the functional and the project.  One extreme is 
so heavily weighted towards the functional so that the project rarely, if 
ever, exists... and these are called (surprise!) Functional Organisations.  
On the other extreme would be a consulting company that takes on tasks for 
companies that just want something done and don't have the in-house 
expertise to implement; the consulting company, doing only project, is 
called the Projectised Organisation.

The weighting of the balance between the two needs in a single 
organisation determines - in NewSpeak - the kind of matrix the 
organisation employs.  When it is weighted towards the functional the 
project manager's needs are subordinate to the functional manager's 
needs... 'We gotta keep the widgets moving' is heavier than 'We gotta 
implement the Widgetzip 9000 system' this is called the 'weak matrix'; 
project managers usually have less authority and are not so much managers 
as co-ordinators.

In a 'strong matrix' organisation the reverse is true; while the widgets 
still have to keep moving the project manager for Widgetzip 9000 has more 
authority over allocation of personnel and resources.

DD
```

On Nov 14, 12:58 pm, docdw...@panix.com () wrote:
> My memory is, admittedly, porous... but the other day I was reminded of
> something that someone posted here and was wondering about how things
…[14 more quoted lines elided]…
> DD

It's been about 8 years since I last logged on here.  I think my last
posts were around the time of Katrina.
Seems much has changed in the world bu the CLC forum has teh same old
characters in it!

I can say that at my time at a rather large company changed for the
worse after becoming matrixed.  (Let's call the company Large Blue).

My experience was that roles become more strictly defined - no one
worked outside of their project or tried to expand their role.  The
idea of "team" went out of the window - you work for people close to
you but not those who live on the other side of the country/world.
You would either (a) Get a project of 50 hrs a week and be told to
claim less overtime, or (b) Get a project of less than 40 hrs a week
and be asked to find additional work (but no one had 5 hr a week
projects).  Ultimately, the matrix model hit the external customer
project and then the issue became "Find me a 40 hr a week resource to
work in Atlanta for a maximum of $23 hr" (this was a REAL posting
internally at the Large Blue company).

Eventually many people got burned out and left or got kicked out.
Many of the "clients" actually came looking for former Large Blue
company employees as it's cheaper to hire an independent consultant
than an independent consultant through Large Blue Projectized
environments.

Anyway.  I've mostly got out of coding now because it bored me (play
around with Drupal/PHP mostly).   Recently picked up a new career
where the strategic development is on a platform running COBOL on
Solaris. I thought COBOL was going away back in 2004 :)  I've been
thinking of starting a company to rewrite it in C# independently -
think it would take 4-5 programmers 2-3 years to get it right but
could probably sell a non-exclusive license for 2-3 million (incl.
support) and there would likely be about 4-5 interested companies.
Too much of a risk for me :)

Glad to see everyone is still out and about in COBOL land :)

JCE.
```

## Thread: ODO's, Dynamic Storage, and Standards — 2 this month / 3 total

_Topics: [`COBOL standards (ANS, ISO, 74/85/2002/2014)`](topics.md#standards)_

_Thread started [2011-10](2011-10.md#t-b881b8a06a)._

#### ↳ Re: ODO's, Dynamic Storage, and Standards

- **From:** Frank Swarbrick <fswarbrick@gmail.com>
- **Date:** 2011-11-16T17:37:00-08:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9957762.784.1321493820581.JavaMail.geo-discussion-forums@yqcm23>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<yDGpq.3519$rt7.441@en-nntp-05.dc1.easynews.com>`
- **References:** `<yDGpq.3519$rt7.441@en-nntp-05.dc1.easynews.com>`

```
What is the date of the latest draft?

Anyway, I think both of these could be quite useful.  Especially for the code I wrote recently.  I know some(!) hate ODO, but I've found it to be of great value, if somewhat awkward.  Basically, I've used it to "simulate" the "dynamic length elementary items".  Or really the "any length" data items; I'm not sure that these are the same...

The simplest example is this: a routine can be called with a text string that varies in length.  So the call might look like this:

PERFORM WITH TEST AFTER UNTIL DONE-SW = 'Y'
    COMPUTE MY-CHUNK-LEN = CONTENT FUNCTION LENGTH(MY-CHUNK)
    CALL MY-SUBR USING MY-STRING, CONTENT FUNCTION LENGTH(MY-STRING)
                       MY-CHUNK, MY-CHUNK-LEN
                 RETURNING DONE-SW
    DISPLAY '(' MY-CHUNK (1:MY-CHUNK-LEN) ')'
END-PERFORM

(I actually use "LENGTH OF MY-STRING" instead of "FUNCTION LENGTH(MY-STRING)", so I'm not 100% sure the latter is supported, but I believe LENGTH OF is an IBM extension).

The subroutine has code like this:

WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
77  PS-POS            PIC S9(9) COMP-5 VALUE 1.
77  DONE-SW           PIC X VALUE 'N'.
    88  DONE                VALUE 'Y'.
77  CHUNK-MAX         PIC S9(9) COMP-5 VALUE ZERO.

LINKAGE SECTION.
01  PASSED-STRING.
    05  PIC X OCCURS 0 TO 9876 DEPENDING ON PASSED-STR-LEN.
77  PASSED-STR-LEN    PIC S9(9) COMP-5.
01  CHUNK.
    05  PIC X OCCURS 0 TO 500 DEPENDING ON CHUNK-LEN.
77  CHUNK-LEN         PIC S9(9) COMP-5.
77  IS-DONE           PIC X.
PROCEDURE DIVISION USING PASSED-STRING, PASSED-STR-LEN
                         CHUNK, CHUNK-LEN
                   RETURNING IS-DONE.
    IF CHUNK-MAX = ZERO
        MOVE CHUNK-LEN TO CHUNK-MAX
    END-IF
    IF NOT DONE
        PERFORM PARSE-STRING
    END-IF
    MOVE DONE-SW TO IS-DONE
    GOBACK.

PARSE-STRING.
    MOVE CHUNK-MAX TO CHUNK-LEN
    MOVE SPACES TO CHUNK
    UNSTRING PASSED-STRING DELIMITED BY X'19'
             INTO CHUNK CNT CHUNK-LEN
             WITH POINTER PS-POS
    NOT ON OVERFLOW
        SET DONE TO TRUE
    END-UNSTRING
    PERFORM HANDLE-CHUNK
    .

HANDLE-CHUNK.
    DISPLAY QUOTE CHUNK QUOTE
    .

I'm out of time at the moment, but I do want to point out the usefulness in this case of ODO.  Both the UNSTRING of PASSED-STRING and and the DISPLAY of CHUNK work beautifully with it; very readable.  If not for it I'd have to explicitly use reference modification, which while useful, would not be nearly as elegant in this case.

Tomorrow(?) I will post how I imagine this would look with recent enhancements to COBOL in the standard.

Frank
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: ODO's, Dynamic Storage, and Standards

- **From:** "HeyBub" <heybub@NOSPAMgmail.com>
- **Date:** 2011-11-18T05:03:51-06:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<gsqdnaC3gdoHplvTnZ2dnUVZ_hKdnZ2d@earthlink.com>`
- **References:** `<yDGpq.3519$rt7.441@en-nntp-05.dc1.easynews.com> <9957762.784.1321493820581.JavaMail.geo-discussion-forums@yqcm23>`

```
Frank Swarbrick wrote:
> What is the date of the latest draft?
>
…[73 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Looks like you're taking a string and deconstructing it into paragraphs.

I've never used the below code, but it seems as if it would work:

01  CHUNK-LEN  PIC S9(4) COMP-5.
01  CHUNK  PIC X(3000).
01  UNSTRING-PTR  PIC S9(4) COMP-5.

MOVE 1 TO UNSTRING-PTR
PERFORM UNTIL UNSTRING-PTR > STRING-LEN
  MOVE 0 TO CHUNK-LEN
  MOVE SPACE TO CHUNK
  UNSTRING MYSTRING INTO CHUNK DELIMITED BY X'19'
    WITH POINTER UNSTRING-PTR
    TALLYING IN CHUNK-LEN
  PERFORM PROCESS-CHUNK
END-PERFORM

You COULD exit the perform as soon as you see a blank CHUNK, but that would 
fail if you hit two CRs in a row.
```

## Thread: Object-oriented extensions? — 2 this month / 4 total

### Object-oriented extensions?

- **From:** axtens <bruce.axtens@gmail.com>

#### ↳ Re: Object-oriented extensions?

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2011-11-19T12:03:28+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<9io6ibFngkU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<ea681fb1-f933-454e-a6b8-5a3bd36f8c1f@h31g2000pro.googlegroups.com>`

```
axtens wrote:
> Sorry if I'm repeating myself here, but is there a timeframe in which
> I might expect to see the object-oriented extensions to COBOL
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> Bruce.

Hi Bruce,

I don't think there has ever been a committment from the OC team to provide 
OO COBOL.

It's a question of focus and priorities. And these, in turn, are pretty much 
dictated by demand from the user community.

COBOLlers generally are not interested in object oriented programming.

OC is a pretty huge undertaking and they have done a very good job of it, 
but actually implementing OO would be a major effort.

I asked Roger about 18 months ago if there would be OO support and, although 
he didn't rule it out long term, it was not something on their horizion at 
that time.

If it is ever implemented I would be glad to use it as part of the Migration 
Tools.

Perhaps you could ask them directly by posting your question to their user 
forum?

Pete.
```
